Mr. and Mrs. Fernand van der Straeten Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday 109

This Morning, Hosting Chinese and Foreign Journalists

Planned Trip to Hangzhou and Other Places for Sightseeing

Mr. Fernand van der Straeten and his wife, a leader of the Second International and former Minister of Foreign Affairs of Belgium, arrived in Shanghai at 3:00 PM yesterday on the Nagasaki Maru from Kobe, Japan. Representatives from various organizations welcomed them at the Wharf. Mr. Van der Straeten is a leader of the Belgian Socialist Party and a man of vast learning. At the invitation of the Academia Sinica, he is visiting China for travel and lecturing. He arrived in Beijing and Tianjin earlier this month and then went to Japan for sightseeing, where he was warmly welcomed by people from all walks of life. Details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

Representatives from various organizations who welcomed them at the Wharf yesterday included Xu Juefu representing Cai Yuanpei.

Photography of Mr. and Mrs. Fernand van der Straeten Arriving in Shanghai

(Photo taken by this Newspaper)

From left to right: Mr. and Mrs. Fernand van der Straeten and Belgian Minister Mr. Wouters

Chen Shiguang, Director of the Foreign Affairs Office; Liu Yunfang; Chen Kecheng, Secretary of the Municipal Government; Wang Xun of the Local Court; Gong Xianming of the Association of Belgian Students; Nong Ruhui of the Sino-French Industrial School; Peng Xiang of Labor University; Yang Xiaoshu of the Science Society of China; Zhu Shaoping of the Chinese Students' Association; Belgian Minister Mr. Wouters; Mr. Schevenels, Counselor of the Belgian Embassy; and about fifty other people, including representatives from various organizations and Chinese and foreign journalists. After the Nagasaki Maru docked, the welcoming personnel boarded the ship one after another and shook hands with Mr. and Mrs. Van der Straeten. Then, Zhu Shaoping, Nong Ruhui, and others escorted the couple directly to their residence at the Sino-Western Sanatorium for rest.

Mr. Van der Straeten's Remarks

Although weary from the journey and advanced in years, Mr. Van der Straeten was still very energetic. He smiled and mingled with Chinese and foreign journalists on board, showing no signs of fatigue. He also spoke English very fluently, although he suffered from some hearing loss. When asked about his stay in Shanghai and his future travel plans, he replied that he could not provide any information as he had not yet consulted with the relevant parties. When Japanese journalists asked about his impressions of his visits to Tokyo, Osaka, Kobe, and other places in Japan, he gestured frequently to express his admiration, saying that the rapid and great material progress of their country was truly admirable. Finally, when asked how old he was, he replied sixty-three.

Hosting Journalists

Mr. Van der Straeten is scheduled to host Chinese and foreign journalists this morning. The Shanghai International Reception Committee notified the newspapers yesterday, saying, "Mr. Fernand van der Straeten, former Foreign Minister of Belgium and Chairman of the Second International, arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru on the 29th. A reception for Chinese and foreign journalists will be held at the Foreign Affairs Discussion Hall at 11:00 AM on Tuesday, September 30th. Your presence will be greatly appreciated. Also, tonight at 8:00 PM, various organizations will hold a public banquet for Mr. and Mrs. Van der Straeten at the Grand China Hotel."

Subsequent Itinerary

According to news from the Belgian Embassy, Mr. and Mrs. Van der Straeten are scheduled to visit Hangzhou for sightseeing on the 1st, return to Shanghai on the morning of the 4th, attend a luncheon hosted by the Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee, and attend a banquet hosted by Belgian Minister Wouters and his wife at the Cathay Hotel in the evening. On the 5th, Minister Wang Jingqi will host a luncheon, and Mr. Van der Straeten will deliver a speech at the Chamber of Commerce in the afternoon. In the evening, the Belgian Consul will host a banquet. On the 6th, the Chamber of Commerce will host a banquet in the evening. On the 7th, they will go to Beijing. It is not yet decided whether they will go to Hankou. After returning to Shanghai, they also plan to visit Hong Kong and Annam.

Arrival in China

A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency met with Wang Jingqi, the former Belgian Minister, yesterday. According to him, when he was about to leave his post in Belgium last year and return to China, Mr. Van der Straeten expressed to him in his personal capacity that he wished to travel to China, but as he was a scholar, he was short of funds and hoped that China could provide assistance. When he returned to China and arrived in Beijing, the Belgian Minister again conveyed this wish. He then applied to the Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee in his personal capacity for assistance for Mr. Van der Straeten. It was finally decided that Mr. Van der Straeten would be invited to China to lecture in the name of the Academia Sinica. Mr. Wang also said that the abolition of unequal treaties actually began in Belgium. The Sino-Belgian Commercial Treaty was signed in the fourth year of the Tongzhi reign. The treaty stipulated that if neither party proposed amendments, it could be extended for ten years. If a new treaty was not concluded, the old treaty would continue to be valid. Therefore, the treaty was repeatedly delayed for another sixty years after its expiration. In the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, the entire country unanimously urged the abolition of the Belgian treaty. After the vigorous negotiations of former Foreign Minister Gu Weijun and himself, Belgium finally agreed to abolish the treaty. Both parties agreed to abolish the old treaty. In terms of tariffs, Belgium would still enjoy the treatment of the most favored nation, and the abolition of Belgian consular jurisdiction in China was also agreed upon. This matter was finally concluded. Mr. Van der Straeten was the Belgian Foreign Minister at the time, so we have a lot of goodwill towards him, and so on.

Rice Prices Falling, Not Rising 110

Removal of Rice Price Limits in North Shanghai

Registration and Evaluation Abolished Simultaneously

The rice market in this city has become even more sluggish in recent days. The best Xin Geng rice has already opened below 16 yuan. The North Shanghai Office of the Rice and Bean Industry Association previously reported to the Bureau of Social Affairs that the Chen Po Geng rice was scarce and would soon disappear, while the supply of new rice was abundant, the stock was quite large, and sales were slow. Prices were falling rather than rising, and the period of panic had passed. They requested the cancellation of registration and evaluation procedures. It is reported that the Bureau of Social Affairs, having observed that the price limits had been in place for six months and finding the claims to be true, has approved the cancellation of both the price limits and the registration in North Shanghai from October 1st.

Water Company Implements Account Audit Yesterday 111

Until the Audit is Complete

Water Bills will be Paid According to Old Regulations

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association is seeking a proper solution to the water price increase by the Shanghai Municipal Council Waterworks. The fifth Executive Committee specially appointed Yu Xiji, He Dekui, and Pan Xulun as representatives to go to the Water Company to inspect the accounts of previous years as a basis for determining whether or not to increase prices. Yesterday at 2:30 PM, the three representatives went to the company to audit the accounts. (Mr. Yu Xiji arrived from Beijing yesterday morning.) They were received and welcomed by the company's General Manager Paulsen, Secretary Walter, and Auditor Klingener, who showed a humble attitude and immediately submitted the accounts for the previous six months for inspection. The representatives requested to see the company's operating reports for the past fifteen years, as well as balance sheets and income statements. The company initially hesitated, but after explanations, they agreed. The representatives planned to spend a week going to the company every day for the audit. Yesterday, they audited the financial statements for the first half of this year, and today they will begin reviewing the previous accounts. The correspondence between the Ratepayers' Association and the Water Company is compiled as follows:

Water Company's Letter to the Ratepayers' Association

Regarding your letter of the 25th of this month, we have learned that your association has appointed Yu Xiji, Pan Xulun, He Dekui, and three other gentlemen as representatives to review the accounts on which the proposed 25% surcharge is based. We would like to know when your representatives will arrive. The last paragraph of your letter refers to the minutes of the Shanghai Municipal Council meeting on September 17th. According to the minutes, a certain director proposed the formation of a committee to investigate whether the price increase was necessary, but this was not approved. It was only passed that your association be informed that our company's accounts can be publicly reviewed. From this point of view, the suggestion in your letter to suspend the collection of water bills by our company is not only useless but also impossible at this time. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association.

Ratepayers' Association's Reply to the Water Company

Regarding your letter of September 20th, regarding the appointment of representatives to meet with you for the audit, the representatives appointed to audit your company have scheduled to perform this task within the next week. Please take note. As for the collection of water bills, our association believes that before the audit is completed and it is determined that a price increase is warranted, your company should only charge 6%, that is, charge at the original price. If it is later determined that a price increase is warranted, the difference can be collected retroactively. The minutes of the Shanghai Municipal Council meeting on September 17th have already been reviewed. The Council's approach is indeed appropriate, as it is well aware that it is practically impossible to express fairness regarding the price increase without having your company's accounts reviewed by our association. Regarding this point, we hope your company will pay attention to it. We reply accordingly, hoping you will take note that water prices should continue to be charged at the original price before the audit is completed and it is determined that a price increase is warranted, in order to avoid disputes.

Ratepayers' Association's Letter to the Real Estate Association

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association sent a letter to the Real Estate Association yesterday, saying, "Regarding the Shanghai Waterworks Company's letter of September 27th, stating that water prices should be charged at the new price regardless of the outcome of the audit, our association immediately replied to the company, 'Regarding the collection of water bills, our association believes that before the audit is completed and it is determined that a price increase is warranted, your company should only charge 6%, that is, charge at the original price. If it is later determined that a price increase is warranted, the difference can be collected retroactively,' and so on. We inform you accordingly, hoping you will take note and immediately notify that all water bills should be paid at the old rate before the audit is completed and it is determined that a price increase is warranted.

County Government Held County Political Meeting Yesterday 116

48th Meeting

The Shanghai County Government held its 48th County Political Meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included the heads of various bureaus, the Director of Property Management, and the section chief of the County Government Secretariat. County Magistrate Yan chaired the meeting, and Hu Gongshou recorded the minutes. (2) The County Construction Bureau proposed that the first phase of land prices for the land acquired for the North Hui Road be directly issued by the Finance Bureau. The resolution was to hand it over to the Finance and Construction Bureaus for joint handling. The resolution was that the prohibition measures should be handled in accordance with the regulations issued by the Provincial Department, and the registration regulations were amended and passed. Joint Defense of Shanghai, Songjiang, Nanhui, and Fengxian Counties 117

The Shanghai, Songjiang, Nanhui, and Fengxian Counties Joint Defense Committee held its second preparatory meeting in Shanghai the day before yesterday (28th). Attendees included Yan Shenyu, County Magistrate of Shanghai County; Shen Jinghua, Director of the Public Security Bureau; Ye Dezhen, Secretary; Jin Qingzhang, County Magistrate of Songjiang County; Zhang Qianshou, Director of the Public Security Bureau; Kong Chong, County Magistrate of Nanhui County; Shen Qingchen, County Magistrate of Fengxian County; and Lin Changzong, representative of Chi Chen Zekuan, Director of the First District of the Jiangsu Water Police. After the meeting, Yan Shenyu chaired the meeting, and Ye Dezhen recorded the minutes. The discussion of the proposals was entirely related to military secrets. The general measures are said to be: (1) The names of the police regiment commanders at the junction of the two counties should be notified to each other in advance. (2) Joint patrols will be conducted. (3) In the event of a bandit alarm, there will be mutual assistance regardless of territorial boundaries. (4) It was decided that the meeting date of the committee would be the last Sunday of each month. (5) The charter of the Joint Defense Committee was passed. (6) In an emergency, the issued orders can be first sent to the military police, and then to the counties, etc. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM that day. The next meeting will be held in Shanghai on October 26th.

Schools Participate in Anti-Drug Week 122

Special Editions Published in National Newspapers

Preparations for the 7th Anti-Drug Week, which will be held from October 1st to 7th this year, have been repeatedly reported in various newspapers. All sectors of the city are actively participating. The association believes that the academic community is the backbone of society, and the anti-drug movement relies heavily on the academic community. This year's Anti-Drug Week should focus on student education. The Municipal Education Bureau has been requested to instruct all levels of schools to hold anti-drug lectures and post various propaganda materials during Anti-Drug Week to give the academic community a deep understanding of the opium problem. The letters to the Education Bureau and various schools are as follows: (1) Letter to the Education Bureau: "The 7th National Anti-Drug Movement Week this year has been scheduled for October 1st to 7th. All provinces, cities, and counties have already started preparations. Shanghai is a place of interest to both China and foreign countries, and it is an area where opium and drugs are rampant. The Anti-Drug Movement Week needs to be expanded. In order to arouse the interest of the academic community in participating in the anti-drug movement, encourage research on the opium problem, and conduct an anti-drug lecture and essay competition this year, this year's competition is already in active preparation. However, during the anti-drug cycle, the education of the academic community is the most urgent task at present. Our association has sent various pictures, slogans, propaganda outlines, etc. for this year's Anti-Drug Week to various schools, asking them to post them and hold anti-drug lectures in the schools. We hereby request your bureau to instruct all schools to handle this matter together in order to expand propaganda. The future of anti-drug is dependent on it. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau. (2) Letter to the Schools: "The opium disaster in China is deeply and greatly painful. Diplomatic failures, internal affairs are not well-governed, industry is declining, and people's livelihood is difficult. Tracing the origin of the disaster, opium is the main cause of everything. Our association takes promoting the anti-drug movement as its duty, and its purpose is to urge the government to earnestly prohibit smoking, awaken the people, unanimously reject drugs, eliminate the domestic smoking disaster, and stop imported poisons, in order to save the country from danger and seek strength. However, in order to achieve the above-mentioned goals, it is impossible to succeed without expanding anti-drug education and anti-drug propaganda. Therefore, our association has the National Anti-Drug Movement Week every year, notifying comrades across the country, individuals, and sympathetic groups to carry out large-scale anti-drug movements at the same time. The 7th Anti-Drug Week this year has been scheduled for October 1st to 7th by our association. At the time when domestic smoking bans are urgently needed and the International Conference will be held soon, compared with previous years, it is even more necessary to exert all efforts to carry out a more enthusiastic and great movement. We have always admired your school for sympathizing with anti-drug and saving the country. We hereby send you pictures, short chapters, and notices, and we ask you to post them during Anti-Drug Week and hold anti-drug lectures to cultivate the concept of anti-drug among young students and contribute to the unprecedentedly great feat of this year. The future of anti-drug is very fortunate. Sincerely dedicated, respectfully wishing you well." It is also heard that for this Anti-Drug Week, in addition to the newspapers in Shanghai, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, the following newspapers across the country have published special editions: Harbin Business Gazette, Daily News, Harbin Gazette, Binjiang Times, Great Northern News, Northeast China Business News, Changchun Dadong Daily, Yimin Times, Northeast China Times, Heilongjiang Newspaper, Heihe Daily, Changsha Dagong Bao, Chongde Dazhong Daily, Hankou Zhongshan Daily, Shenyang Northeast China Gazette, Jilin Jichang Daily, Shashi Yangtze River Business News, Yichang Times, Hengzhou Xiangjiang Daily, Yichang Yishi Bao, Wuchang Hubei Gazette, Hankou News, Continental News, Wuhu Industrial and Commercial Daily, Wanjiang Daily, Ganzhou Xin Gannan Bao, Sanmin Daily, Weixin Bao, Jiujiang Republic Daily, Jiujiang Evening News, Jiangsheng Daily, Hankou Public Opinion Daily, Chongqing Business News, Nanchang Jiangxi Evening News, Lanzhou Xinlong Daily, Minhou Anti-Drug Review Report, Fuzhou Evening News, Xin Fuzhou Bao, Xinmin Bao, Public Opinion Xinbao, and dozens of other places.

The Silk Factories Still Insist on Suspending Operations to Oppose Public Weighing and Inspection 123

Using Suspension of Business as a Countermeasure

The Shanghai Silk Factories Association, due to various businesses opposing public weighing and inspection, and requesting financial assistance for the silk industry from the Ministry of Finance, continued to hold a general meeting of representatives of all businesses yesterday (the 29th) at 3:00 PM. Executive committee members Zhu Jing'an, Huang Jinchen, Zhang Peishen, Wang Xiaolai, etc., and over ninety manufacturers attended. Chairman Shen Huachen presided, and after formal greetings, the first matter discussed was the opposition by cocoon merchants from Zhejiang Province to the import of Japanese cocoons. The chairman explained the reasons for the opposition from various groups. It was generally agreed that the request to reduce import duties on Japanese cocoons was from June of this year. At that time, due to insufficient domestic supply, it was proposed to purchase Japanese cocoons to make up for the shortfall. Subsequently, due to opposition from various parties, the government had already ordered customs to prohibit the import of Japanese cocoons, so the matter was a thing of the past. Moreover, silk prices had recently fallen, and Japanese cocoon prices were high, making it unprofitable for factories. Shanghai silk factories had not purchased Japanese cocoons, so the matter was no longer an issue and did not need discussion (passed). The next item was the opposition to public weighing and inspection. After Chairman Shen read aloud the full text of the reply from the Bureau of Commodity Inspection, it was generally felt that the reasons given by the bureau were far-fetched and evasive, and it was unwilling to act as an intermediary. At a time when the silk market in foreign firms was declining, and the silk industry was at a critical juncture, silk factories were closing down due to losses. The bureau still wanted factories to bear additional losses, which was truly insensitive to the difficulties of businesses. Moreover, before the previous general meeting, the public weight of silk sent by various factories to the inspection office was more than ten catties less than the net weight. Now, after the general meeting, the public weight inspected was more than ten catties greater than the net weight, and its intention was clear - to alleviate opposition. The businesses must not be fooled. Since the bureau was unwilling to cancel it, the only option was to follow the resolution of the previous meeting. If the bureau did not cancel public weighing and inspection by October 1st, operations would be suspended to fight for it. Chairman Shen suggested that if all businesses suspended operations, tens of thousands of workers would inevitably have no means of livelihood, which was a major issue for the national economy and people's livelihood. He repeatedly advised the representatives to wait for a petition to the Ministry of Finance before deciding on a course of action. However, the manufacturers present were quite indignant and insisted on implementing the resolution of the previous general meeting. Seeing the strong sentiments of the crowd, Chairman Shen was unable to dissuade them. However, for the sake of caution, he put the motion to suspend operations to a vote, and it was unanimously approved twice by standing up. In accordance with the resolution of the previous general meeting, if public weighing and inspection was not cancelled by the deadline, all silk factories in Shanghai would suspend operations together and wait (passed). Finally, the matter of submitting a petition to the government for financial assistance to the silk industry was discussed. Chairman Shen reported that he and the two standing committee members, Wang Xiaolai and Huang Jinchen, had visited Vice Minister Zhang of the Ministry of Finance to request an allocation of public bonds or the issuance of silk industry bonds worth five million yuan to provide assistance. Vice Minister Zhang agreed to discuss the matter further at a later date and would reply after another visit to Vice Minister Zhang the next day. The meeting adjourned after discussions, around 7:00 PM.

Reduced Shipping Rates for Exports to the East Indies 124

Estimated Reduction of Thirty-Five Percent

The Java Shipping Company in this port is gradually expanding its shipping operations in the East Indies. It has a total of three shipping routes, with two regular passenger ships to Java each month, and a non-regular cargo ship every fourteen days. The ships currently in use include the "Chikareng," "Chibadak," "Chishengda," "Chikinbong," "Chimolok," "Chisalak," "Chilibapart," and "Chisailiya," among over ten others. The largest has a capacity of 16,000 tons. To develop the export cargo business from China to the East Indies and the South Seas Islands, it has been decided to implement a reduction in the shipping rates for export cargo departing from Shanghai. The shipping rates will be reduced by sixty-five percent across the board from the original rates. In effect, the reduction is a significant thirty-five percent. The new shipping rates are being revised, and the company has already notified all parties. All goods shipped from Shanghai to Batavia, Semarang, Surabaya, Makassar, and other ports will be subject to the price reduction.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Investigates and Replies Regarding the Custom of Promissory Notes 125

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court yesterday, stating that on the 5th of this month, it received a letter requesting a detailed investigation and reply on two points regarding the custom of using promissory notes in Shanghai in connection with cases being handled. The Chamber immediately forwarded the letter to the Shanghai Money Trade Association for investigation and reply. The reply stated that the Association's members use three types of negotiable instruments: bank drafts, checks, and remittances, but there is no such thing as a "promissory note." As for whether promissory notes can be used for commercial transactions and whether the use of promissory notes can be considered as clear settlement of accounts, the customs vary among different industries, and the Association cannot speculate. At the same time, the Chamber's investigation found that the commercial custom in this city is to use bank drafts or checks for commercial transactions. Bank drafts are subject to a ten-day term as stipulated by the money trade. As for the commonly referred to "promissory notes," they are issued by businesses who temporarily lack cash in their operations, are unable to repay debts, and issue a promissory note as a last resort to indicate to the creditor their responsibility for the debt. The note specifies the period for repayment in installments to indicate the process of clearing the business. The nature of this type of note seems to be a contract between the creditor and the debtor and cannot be considered as clear settlement of accounts. Clear settlement of accounts should only occur after receiving cash or a banker's draft or bank draft from a third party. A corresponding letter is sent for your reference.

Various Associations Uphold Trade Regulations 126

The Shanghai Sausage Association and other groups believe that trade regulations are the lifeblood of the associations. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce recently reviewed the issue of trade regulations and considered them insignificant, which has a great impact on various trade associations. The associations recently sent letters to various public associations, jointly requesting the National Government to instruct the Ministry to re-examine the matter. Yesterday, the Seashore Produce and Green Goods Association replied, stating that upon receiving the letter and a copy of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's reply to the Executive Yuan, they expressed their sympathy. Since the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's review and disapproval of the case where all non-member businesses should comply with the approved trade regulations was published and replied to the Executive Yuan, the morale of the associations has been weakened, and there is a great tendency to disintegrate. The fact that your esteemed Association has requested various public associations to jointly petition the National Government to instruct the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry to re-examine the matter is a matter of life and death for the association. They dare not hesitate to call for a follow-up. This case is based on the spirit of Article 2 of the promulgated Association Law, which is both justified and reasonable. They hope that your esteemed Association will continue to express its sincere and reasoned arguments with an unyielding spirit, and that the associations will jointly submit a petition to the National Government to order the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry to re-examine the matter to achieve the purpose of approval, which is truly a public benefit.

The Jianghai Customs Regularly Burns Confiscated Opium 127

October 3rd

During the 208th term, the Jianghai Customs seized and confiscated nine dan, twenty-one jin, eleven liang, seven qian, and five fen of opium, as well as four thousand seventy-two liang of morphine, and two thousand six dan of poppy shells. In addition, there were morphine-containing pills valued at 1,014 silver dollars. The Superintendent, Mr. Meierhe, reported to the Supervisory Office and scheduled to transport the aforementioned opium, etc., to the kiln in Pudong for burning at 9:00 AM on October 3rd. Yesterday, the Supervisory Office sent letters to the military and political organizations in this port, requesting them to send personnel to supervise the burning.

Industry Unions Are Not Allowed to Handle Labor-Capital or Labor-Labor Disputes 128

The Municipal Training Council Issues a Circular for Compliance

The Mass Training Committee of the Shanghai Special City Party Department stated that the powers of the Preparatory Committee of the Federation of Industry Unions have been clearly stipulated in Article 2 of the organizational rules of each association as (A) the reorganization of the old industry unions, (B) the organization of new industry unions, (C) the registration of industry unions, and (D) other preparatory matters. The work in items A and B of this article should be submitted to the Municipal Training Council for handling according to law. The powers of the instructors of the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions have also been clearly stipulated as 1. guiding the activities of the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions, 2. participating in the meetings of the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions, 3. carrying out the orders of the Municipal Party Department and mediating labor-labor disputes with the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions, 4. examining the thoughts and actions of the staff and members or workers of the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions, and 5. handling matters temporarily designated by this committee. These have all been promulgated. However, it has recently been found that the committees often handle labor-capital disputes or labor-labor disputes of their respective industries on their own, disregarding their own responsibilities. This is inappropriate and exceeds their authority. This situation is considered to require strict correction. Yesterday, a special order was issued to the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions and the industry unions, stating that they must not handle labor-capital disputes or labor-labor disputes on their own in the future, and that the instructors of the preparatory committees of the Federation of Industry Unions must carefully provide guidance and not be negligent.

The Shanghai Java Company Has Not Yet Expressed an Opinion on the Xiao Case 129

But Says That After Verification, He Will Be Sentenced to Imprisonment

The case of the deputy captain of the Shanghai Java Company's ship insulting Ms. Xiao has aroused resistance from various public organizations. Yesterday, the reporter went to the company to inquire whether the Dutch authorities and the shipping company had any concrete measures to express their opinion on the case. According to the person in charge of the company, after Shenbao reported the matter, the Shanghai branch had telegraphed the head office to inquire about the disposal method, but no reply had been received. He also stated that the Netherlands is a country ruled by law and attaches great importance to the law. Since such incidents have been discovered, the authorities will definitely have a way to deal with them. He recalled that several years ago, a case also occurred in Shanghai where a Dutchman serving as a police officer raped a Chinese woman. After the incident was verified, he was sent back to his country and sentenced to eight years in prison, and is still in prison. Now that the deputy captain has insulted the Chinese people in this way, once it is verified, not only will he be dismissed, but he should also be sentenced to imprisonment. Because the head office has not yet sent a telegram, the Shanghai branch is not in a position to express any opinion on this case.

Local News Is Still Transferred to the Back Page 134

Page 11

Local News Two

Jubilant Atmosphere in the Auditorium: Two Newlyweds Suddenly Arrested 135

It Turns Out to Be a Bigamy Drama

The First Wife, Upon Hearing the News, How Can She Bear It?

Guests, Disappointed, Disperse

Yesterday, the Court Ordered Bail

Sipping Tea and Enjoying Music Leads to Intimacy: Zhang Rongfa, an Investigator from the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol, has a daughter named Huifen, also known as Gendi, born in March of the Jia Yin year. Zhang cherishes her like a pearl. When she grows up, he sends her to the Western District Primary School attached to Nanyang Middle School. She is quite intelligent. But she is not yet betrothed. The Zhang family lives outside the Rihui Bridge on Longhua Road and runs the Danfeng Teahouse at home, hiring performers of Su Tan opera to perform every night to attract customers. Zhang Shirong, the owner of the Zhang Bingji tobacco and paper shop in the Xizhalan area of Gaochang Temple nearby, is only twenty-four years old. He regularly visits the Danfeng Teahouse at night to sip tea and enjoy the music. Over time, he becomes intimate with Huifen. She understands romantic feelings. Zhang seduces her and she falls into his trap.

Over Time, They Emulate Hongfu and Eloped: Rongfa sees his beloved daughter whispering sweet nothings with Shirong in public, believing it is not something a daughter should do. He tries to admonish her, but the daughter not only does not listen but also thinks her parents are not understanding enough. In this era of open socializing, children's marriages should have absolute freedom, and no one else should interfere. So she argues with her parents. Rongfa tightens his precautions. Huifen cannot bear it and on the nineteenth day of the old fifth month, emulates Hongfu and elopes with Shirong, temporarily staying at the Nanjing Hotel on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession.

He Has a Wife at Home for Three Years Without Children: Shirong is already married to a woman from the Yang family. They married on September 19th of the sixteenth year and have been married for three years. The Yang woman is a week older than Shirong. Upon hearing that her husband has a romantic affair with another family's daughter, she has repeatedly tried to dissuade him, but Shirong retorts that he has been married to her for three years without any children, leaving the Yang woman helpless. Since his beloved daughter left home, Rongfa knew that she was living with Shirong, but for the sake of his reputation, he tolerated it and did not publicize it. Friends and relatives who knew about it mostly advised him to help them get together. Shirong also thought that what's done is done, so he agreed to Huifen marrying him, but insisted on having a matchmaker to save face.

Choosing an Auspicious Day for the Wedding, Jubilant Atmosphere: Shirong, seeing that his goal has been achieved, immediately hired Chen Yinsheng and Xu Jingqing as matchmakers. They chose the auspicious date of September 27th at 8:00 PM to hold the wedding ceremony. The auditorium was at the Hongqing Restaurant at the intersection of Hubei Road and Guangdong Road. They sent out invitations. Last Saturday, the auspicious day arrived. Both families' friends and relatives went to the Hongqing Restaurant to decorate the auditorium, making it extremely luxurious. As dusk approached, red candles were lit in front of the hall, drums and music filled the air outside, and guests arrived in droves, creating a bustling scene. The groom was dressed in a Western suit, with a fresh flower pinned to his lapel, his face beaming with joy. The bride was also wearing a grand wedding gown, making her even more beautiful.

Police Detectives Arrive Suddenly: Just as the male and female attendants were about to invite the couple to the auditorium, Detectives Zhang Liang and Wang Yingjie from the Old Gate Police Station, along with lawyer Zhu Shuzhen, arrived leisurely. The guests were surprised that the groom had such wide connections, even attracting lawyers and detectives to offer their congratulations.

The Bride and Groom Are Arrested Together: Unexpectedly, a young woman followed the lawyer and detectives. The woman's eyebrows were raised, and her anger was evident. She hurried to the auditorium and reported to the detectives that the groom was her husband. The detectives then arrested the bride and groom together. The guests, witnessing this, realized that Shirong had been accused of bigamy by his first wife. The detectives were ordered to arrest him at this time. They all scattered like frightened birds and animals. It was truly a buzzkill. The wedding certificate and guest book on the table were all taken to the police station and placed in separate custody.

The Police Prosecuted Based on Criminal Law: Yesterday morning, this couple was taken to the Special District Court for trial. Huifen had removed her grand wedding gown and changed into a pink qipao, silk stockings, and leather shoes. Shirong was still in his Western suit. However, because there was not enough time for interrogation in the morning, it was postponed to 2:30 PM. Presiding Judge Zhou interrogated them. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that he was prosecuting based on Article 254 of the Criminal Law and requested an investigation. Shirong's first wife, Yang, stated that her husband had found a new love and abandoned his legitimate wife. Only on Saturday morning did she learn that they were formally getting married, so she entrusted Lawyer Zhu to report to the police station to make the arrest.

The Man Says He Is a Dual Heir, the Woman Willing to Be a Concubine: Under questioning, Zhang Shirong confessed that he had been married to Yang for three years without children. He was the dual heir of his uncle, Zhang Bingkun. After he met Huifen, his uncle advocated for him to marry her. Zhang Huifen confessed that she knew that Shirong already had a wife, but she was voluntarily marrying him and was willing to be a concubine.

Both Were Released on Bail, Rescheduled for Another Hearing: The defendants' lawyers requested a postponement so that both parties could settle out of court. However, the police lawyer expressed strong disapproval of a private settlement, stating that this was a public prosecution and could not be arbitrarily dismissed. Presiding Judge Zhou then ordered both defendants to post 500 yuan bail each and rescheduled the hearing.

A Major Gambling Den Busted in the Russian Relief Association 136

No Chinese People Inside

British, Japanese, and Portuguese Citizens Claimed by Consulates

Russian Gamblers Allowed to Post Bail

Five Employees Released on Bail Pending Trial

The Russian Disabled Veterans Relief Association at 172 Route Ghisi was warned by the Hongkou Police Station for allowing people to gamble. However, the association's leaders ignored the warnings and continued to hold gambling sessions every night. Last Saturday (the 27th) at midnight, Lin, the Western Head of the Hongkou Police Station, and Smith, the Western Detective Chief, visited the association for investigation. At the time, people upstairs and downstairs were gambling loudly. The gambling method involved placing a box-shaped object on a table, with one person in charge of rotating the mechanism. When the mechanism rotated, a ball would fall out of the box, with numbers on it. A blackboard was also hung on the wall, with numbers written on it. Gamblers could choose a number and bet on it. If the number they bet on matched the number on the ball, they would win. When the ball was shaken out, one person would shout out the number, and another would verify the number. The organization was quite organized. Besides this gambling method, there were other gambling tools, but they were not popular with the Chinese. So that night, all the gamblers were foreigners. A total of 58 people were arrested upstairs, along with various gambling tools and chips, and taken to the police station for questioning. Among them were 19 Japanese, 5 British, and 1 Portuguese woman. That night, they were handed over to the consulates of Japan, Britain, and Portugal for investigation. The remaining 33 were all of Russian nationality. Russia had no consular jurisdiction, so they were subject to the Special District Court. The police chief arrested five of them: Foshilin, Temilifu, Yier Ying, Ximing, and Shakao Kaofu. The other 28 were all gamblers and were allowed to be released on bail of 30 yuan each. Yesterday morning, the police lawyer, Li Zhishan, filed a lawsuit with the Special Court's Local Court, accusing the former five of violating Articles 279 and 280 of the Criminal Law for running a gambling den, and the latter of violating Article 278 of the Criminal Law for gambling. Presiding Judge Feng interrogated them. According to the report of Police Chief Lin, Foshi Lin was the clerk of the gambling den, Temi and Yi were in charge of shaking the gambling tools in the gambling den downstairs, and Xi and Sha were the receptionists of the gambling den. When they entered the venue, Temi was shaking the gambling tools and announcing the numbers, Yi was checking the numbers, and Sha was issuing chips in the gambling den upstairs. The gambling table upstairs was green, and more than 20 gamblers were there. The gambling den's profit was 10% of the winnings. The police had heard about it for a long time, but because the details were unclear, they sent undercover gamblers to investigate and find out the details before making the arrest the night before. The gambling tools and gambling books were also presented. The five defendants, Foshi Lin, etc., hired lawyers to defend them and requested bail. Presiding Judge Feng approved the five defendants to post 1,000 yuan cash bail each, and the remaining Xuelifu, etc., to post 30 yuan bail each and reschedule the hearing.

To See the Zhejiang Tide, You Must Go to Eight Forts 140

East Tide and South Tide, Extremely Spectacular

The China Travel Service has been organizing Haining tide-watching tours for many years, and its achievements are well known. This year, it has also launched an Eight Forts tide-watching tour to provide mental enjoyment for those who have not seen or have already seen the Zhejiang tide. According to Mr. Tang of the company, he has been to Eight Forts five or six times and has seen tides that are all strange, majestic, and more spectacular than those in Haining. When the tide comes to Eight Forts, it is divided into two types: the East Tide and the South Tide. The South Tide comes before the East Tide. When the two tides meet, they collide, agitate, and splash, creating waves that can be several feet high. As the saying goes, "When it comes, it is like ten thousand horses galloping and thousands of troops shouting. When it goes, it is like a snow mountain collapsing and a silver cliff falling down." It is shocking and terrifying, like a group of tigers chasing sheep. Eight Forts is about ten miles east of Haining. Cars can go directly there. It is heard that the company has built a high enclosure on the cement dike in Eight Forts, with seating for four or five hundred people. From October 5th to the 10th, it will provide dozens of new-style small cars every day to travel between Hangzhou and Eight Forts, with comfortable and fast seating.

Japan Strives to Eradicate Leprosy 142

According to the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun, the Japanese government has always paid close attention to leprosy and has recently formulated a concrete plan to completely eliminate leprosy in the country in thirty years. It will also allocate 700,000 yen from the national treasury every year. In seventeen years, with interest, there will be a total of 37 million yen, which will be sufficient for application. The initial method is to build a very large leprosarium near the Kusatsu hot spring, which can accommodate about 1,000 people. The construction cost is about 1 million yen and is scheduled to be completed within the next three years. It is heard that the Japanese Empress Dowager greatly appreciates this plan and intends to donate a large sum of money in her personal name to promote it.

The Cause of Liang Ruichu's Death is Unclear 150

The Family Requested an Exemption from Autopsy and Was Approved

Liang Ruichu, a Cantonese man from 452 Zhapu Road, Hongkou, was forty-eight years old and had a weak constitution with symptoms of mental frailty. When he was ill, his limbs would tremble. Someone advised him to drink Liangyixuan's specially made three-snake medicinal wine to cure it. Liang was happy to hear this, so he started drinking three-snake wine instead of other kinds of wine a few days ago. At 6:00 PM the night before last, Liang's family members were having dinner, but Liang drank three-snake wine alone. After drinking half a glass, his expression suddenly changed, and he suddenly became unable to speak. His wife, Li, and his son, Jinghong, took him to Tongren Hospital, but the doctors could not diagnose him. His illness worsened rapidly, and he died at 2:00 AM yesterday. The hospital notified the police, who ordered detectives to investigate and took the body to the Autopsy Office on Feilun Road. At 10:00 AM yesterday, Xu Mei, a prosecutor commissioned by the Special District Court, arrived at the office to inspect the body. According to the Western Deputy Chief, the circumstances of the death were quite bizarre, and the police could not investigate the cause of death. However, the deceased had drunk three-snake wine in the last few minutes before his death, so they suspected that the wine was suspicious and requested that the wine be examined. The three-snake wine was presented for inspection. Then, the wife of the deceased, Li, filed a case requesting exemption from autopsy. Mr. Xu agreed that since the family requested exemption from autopsy, the court did not need to do so. He then ordered that the death of Liang Ruichu was due to illness and that the body be handed over to his son, Liang Jinghong, for coffining. According to the autopsy performed by the court doctor, the deceased was bleeding from the mouth, which appeared to be death by poisoning.

Homicide Suspect Arrested in Shanghai 153

Gu Achuan, a 44-year-old tenant farmer from Baijia Township, Liuhe Town, Taicang, had once come to Shanghai several years ago to work as a worker in a foreign-owned yarn factory. After neglecting his duties, he was recommended by a friend to work as a tea server in a small inn. Two years ago, due to physical weakness, he could not fulfill his duties and returned to Liuhe to guard his land, experiencing extreme hardship. He was married to a woman named Lu, who was 45 years old and of a promiscuous nature. She and a fellow villager named Gu Yunzhou (45 years old), also a tenant farmer in Liuhe, had been having an affair for nearly ten years. Last year, around September of the lunar calendar, Gu Yunzhou came to Shanghai, working various hard labor jobs such as operating bellows, selling dried tofu, and working as a road construction worker. Unexpectedly, on February 12th of this year in the lunar calendar, Gu Achuan was murdered by Lu and her stepbrother Xu Asheng (Lu's biological mother was a remarried woman married to Xu Asheng's father) in a joint plot. While Lu and Xu have already been arrested by the Taicang County government for interrogation and detention, Gu Yunzhou, having had an affair with Lu for many years, could not escape significant suspicion. The county magistrate repeatedly ordered the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau to arrest and bring him to justice for questioning. Bureau Chief Yu Keng then specially dispatched police officer Cui Shuren on September 23rd, carrying a letter to Shanghai to search for and arrest him everywhere. The day before yesterday afternoon, the police officer received a tip, stating that Gu Yunzhou was currently hiding in the Yilou Teahouse near the Nanyang Bridge in the French Concession. The police officer sent a letter to the teahouse to inquire, but Gu happened to be nearby, discovered the situation, and fled towards Zhaozhou Road in the Chinese district. He was spotted by police officer Wang Yinzhu of the Second District General Office, who was on patrol. Suspecting his behavior, Wang detained him. At the same time, the police officer sent from Taicang also arrived upon hearing the news and presented the original letter. After careful examination by District Chief Wang, Gu directly admitted to having an affair with Achuan's wife for many years, but absolutely denied plotting to murder Achuan. Officer Cui requested to take him back to Taicang for investigation. District Chief Wang submitted a document to the Judicial Section yesterday for instructions.

American firm Schenk & Mertz apologizes to Chen Zixun in writing

Schenk & Mertz, due to outstanding payments for machinery supplied to the Hengda Yarn Factory, had repeatedly filed lawsuits with the former Provisional Court and the Shanghai Local Court, involving Chen Zixun, manager of the Henglong Bank and representative of the creditor group. However, Schenk & Mertz, having included Mr. Chen as a defendant in the criminal lawsuit due to a misunderstanding, specifically issued a letter to Mr. Chen to express their apologies, hoping to restore good relations. The translation of the original letter is provided below:

To Mr. Chen Zixun,

Regarding the lawsuit between Schenk & Mertz and the Hengda Yarn Factory, now, thanks to the friendly intervention of Mr. Xie Hengchuang, Mr. Mu Ouchu, Mr. Wu Linshu, Mr. Yao Mulian, Mr. Lu Bohong, and Mr. Yuan Ludeng, a satisfactory resolution has been reached, which is truly gratifying. Our firm now understands that the cause of this case was entirely due to misleading statements made by Mr. Mu Shuzhai to you and the public nomination of you by the creditors as their agent. As a result, our firm had no choice but to file a criminal lawsuit with the Provisional Court, including you as one of the defendants, which is extremely regrettable. Our appointed legal counsel has already petitioned the courts to withdraw all parts of the civil, criminal, and appeal aspects of this case, in order to reach a peaceful resolution. We sincerely hope that the friendship between both parties can be restored as before.

Sincerely,

Fulenchu, Representative of Schenk & Mertz

Death of Tea Server Without Doctor's Certificate 155

Requires Examination by the Local Court

Shen Fasheng, a 49-year-old tea server from Minhang working at the Lianyi Silk Weaving Factory on Guohuo Road, died yesterday. Letters to the Editor 168

To the Editor,

I read in your newspaper's "Local News" column on September 21st an article titled "The Triad Gang is Active," which stated, "The Weihai captain is relatively astute." I was formerly the chief engineer of the Weihai warship and an instructor at the torpedo training school, not the captain. This is factually incorrect. I am writing to request a correction.

Sincerely,

Wu Jian

September 29th

To the Editor,

Upon investigation, I found that in a news item published in your newspaper's "Local News" column on July 14th, there was a phrase "Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee of the Overseas Chinese Federation of the Republic of China." The Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee is located in Nanjing and belongs to the party and government organs. Our association is located in Shanghai and belongs to the mass organizations. The nature is completely different. Our association has been organized under the direct orders of the Prime Minister since the first year of the Republic of China and has been named "Overseas Chinese Federation." It has never had the name "Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee." The news on that day was presumably an error by an outside contributor, and our association was completely unaware of it. The descriptions are also inconsistent with the facts. Our association did not read it at the time, so we were unable to correct it in a timely manner. Fortunately, someone informed us, and we finally found and read it in the newspaper pile. We are writing to request that your newspaper publish this letter in the corrections column. We would be extremely grateful.

Respectfully,

Overseas Chinese Federation

Yongchang Pawnshop

Free Talk

Dismissed with a Laugh 169

— Seafarer

Umbrella Vendor: Sir, would you like to buy an umbrella? It can shield you from the rain on rainy days and the sun on sunny days. It's truly a win-win.

Gentleman: I don't want to buy any more umbrellas. Every time I buy one, someone steals it.

Umbrella Vendor: Sir, buy this one. I guarantee it won't be stolen because I've been peddling it for over half a year, and no one wants it.

Father: Child, no matter what knowledge or skill you learn, you must start from the bottom and come up step by step to achieve success.

Son: Father, then when I learn to swim, must I also start from the bottom and first immerse myself in the water?

Wife: Dear, could you possibly help a poor woman? She wants to accompany her son to the park, but she has no new clothes to wear.

Husband: Who is this poor woman? If I'm familiar with her, then we can discuss it.

Wife: You've known this poor woman for over ten years. It's me!

Beggar: Sir, please do a good deed and give me a copper coin. I guarantee you'll have good luck this year and have a big, fat son.

Gentleman: Don't bother me. I never give money to beggars on the street.

Beggar: Then please come to my office and contact my secretary.

A Brief Account of the Public Memorial Ceremony for Mr. Zeng Nongran 170

— Candle Boy

Mr. Zeng Nongran of Hengyang, with his integrity and literary talent, was highly respected in his time. In recent years, he sought refuge in Shanghai, supporting himself by selling his calligraphy. Unfortunately, he passed away on August 27th. Mr. Zeng had students all over the world. His death was deeply mourned by all. A public memorial ceremony was held at Mr. Zeng's residence on Dongyouheng Road on the afternoon of the 25th of the month. Those who attended included Zhang Shanzi, Huang Xiaoting, Li Jianchu, Ma Qizhou, Zhu Dake, Jiang Wanping, Mi Zhemin, Yao Yunjiang, Xu Guanqun, Jiang Yiping, Zhang Jifeng, Ma Zonghuo, Liu Junying, Xie Weifan, and Xiang Moan. The ceremony was presided over by Mr. Zhao Yangjiao, an old friend of Mr. Zeng, and the eulogy was read by Zeng Yiyun. Incense was offered and wine was poured, and the ceremony was conducted with proper etiquette. After the ceremony, the gentlemen initiated the organization of an alumni association. Anyone who had studied under Mr. Zeng was welcome to join. Memorial ceremonies would be held twice a year, in spring and autumn. The gentlemen's deep remembrance of Mr. Zeng and their dedication to honoring him demonstrated Mr. Zeng's careful guidance and enduring love for others. The eulogy was written by Mr. Ma Zonghuo. Its classical and simple style was truly masterful. It is appended here to glimpse Mr. Zeng's scholarship and character.

The Loushan Mountain, truly the southern boundary.

The Cheng flows from its belly, the Xiang passes its tail.

Holding pearls and nurturing jade, pregnant with heng and carrying zhi.

Things are not uniquely endowed, philosophers are enlightened.

What is enlightenment? Mr. exemplifies it.

His sagacious nature is innate, his filial piety and friendship are heavenly.

Born with a precocious nature, his mother is the source.

Sipping snow and eating wind, his form relies on the shadows.

He broadcast his outstanding reputation, shaking the algae in the village school.

Ascending to the capital, he entered the imperial court.

Serving the emperor, he raised the masses.

He did not indulge in good fortune, but praised his mother's chastity.

Suddenly, national changes occurred, and the mother's shadow withered.

The land had no spirit, the heavens had no mercy.

Thus he untied his worldly ties and returned to his original state.

He lived in strict poverty and placed his pride in the pine and bamboo.

Autumn searched and spring stretched, smoke flowed and the moon was solemn.

A single touch could bring joy, his solitary fragrance bloomed.

Then there was a good invitation to travel.

Walking along the river and crossing the lake, pointing east to the sea.

Elders gathered and stopped, their hearts resonating.

It was said to be a refuge, but it also expressed their worries.

Since then, he lived in leisure, not associating with the nobles of the time.

His body was in harmony, and his relationship with others was as strong as gold and stone.

He encompassed the nine streams and extensively summarized the arts.

Whether it was poetry or prose, calligraphy or painting.

His poetry emphasized meaning, not confined to one school.

It was as light as the clouds and as beautiful as the afterglow.

He often said that with distant scenery, why should there be extravagant words?

His prose was as high as the Han dynasty, half-cutting and sharp.

His writing was profound and his meaning was pure.

Rebuilding Ban and Cai, he almost resisted.

The world loves it, and especially loves calligraphy.

The clerical script is square and round, the upright stands and the cursive trends.

The mountain is strict, the sea is abundant, the horse leaps and the ape grasps.

Looking up to Zhong and Wang, looking down on Ou and Yu.

Late in life, he began painting, his spirit connecting with his thoughts.

A foot of silk contained ten thousand miles, an inch of heart contained a thousand folds.

Clouds gathered and trees mixed, water surrounded and mountains overlapped.

Holding a brush, he was distant, I was the law.

Encompassing these four wonders, like silk on a loom.

A person has one of them, and it is enough to be proud.

Only our teacher, humble and respectful and tall.

Embracing the new with transformation, answering questions without tiring.

His remaining glory is far away, and his hidden virtue is more magnificent.

Looking at him, they come to worship, malaria and opportunity.

Ren and Shou only heard, dragons and snakes were doomed.

Hou Yan was still warm, listening to the sound was swift.

Who said a hundred years, vanished in an instant?

What was the fault of the medicine? Heaven was the true culprit.

Alas, alas! The strong wind blows in the evening, and the dew is thick in the morning.

How far away is the teacher? Who is happy for him?

Once received a cane, now offer a cup.

May words be forever cherished, tears overflowing.

Writing to send grief, grieve for its exhaustion.

Alas, alas!

The Remote Striking Technique of the Monks of Tianning Temple 171

— Chunfan

It is said that in Bagua Palm there is a "隔小掌" (gé xiǎo zhǎng, "separated small palm") technique, which can strike a person from a hundred paces away. It can even penetrate a wall. The Northern Chinese colloquialism calls it "隔山打牛" (gé shān dǎ niú, "striking an ox across the mountain") or "百步打空" (bǎi bù dǎ kōng, "striking emptiness from a hundred paces").

During the late Qing dynasty, there was a monk named Pu Yin at Huguo Temple in Changzhou. He was originally a notorious thief, capable of robbing lone travelers dozens or even hundreds of miles away at night or before dawn. After the robbery, he would return to the temple as if carried by the wind. Traveling dozens of miles only took a moment. Therefore, the monks in the temple did not suspect Pu Yin of being a thief.

Once, before dawn, Pu Yin robbed a traveler near Benniu. The traveler had 200 yuan in silver with him, intending to sell soybeans in Changzhou. He was traveling in the dark when he was robbed by Pu Yin. Fortunately, the traveler had an extraordinary gift: once he saw someone, he could recognize them for life. Although their faces were not easily distinguishable in the starlight, he had already silently memorized them in his mind, knowing that it was a monk.

After Pu Yin robbed him of the 200 yuan, he fled swiftly. The traveler trudged to the city, intending to seek help from relatives and friends. He also wanted to visit various temples to find this thieving monk. He first went to the dining hall of Huguo Temple. The monks were having breakfast. The traveler suddenly saw Pu Yin and recognized him as the thief. However, he dared not reveal it immediately. He went to the abbot and told him. The abbot was shocked and quickly sent Pu Yin away. He then searched his luggage and found the stolen goods still there.

The abbot wanted to capture him, but he knew that Pu Yin's martial arts were extremely high and he was not easy to capture. He sought help from the abbot of Tianning Temple. The abbot sent two old monks to help. Before they left, the abbot warned them, "Although you two are skilled in martial arts, it is not certain whether you are superior to Pu Yin. I guess that when you arrive, he will break through the roof to escape. When he breaks through the roof, you must judge by the curvature of his knees. If he bends his knees as he goes up, you can capture him. If he doesn't bend and goes straight, then you cannot defeat him." The two monks agreed and set off.

They arrived at Huguo Temple together. They first sat in the dining hall to wait. Soon, all the monks arrived. As the monks were eating, the traveler suddenly entered, pointed at Pu Yin, and said, "This is the thief who robbed me of 200 yuan!" The abbot shouted sternly, "Capture him!" Pu Yin had already sprung up in response, breaking through the roof to escape. However, his knees did not bend. The two monks from Tianning Temple also flew up from the hole in the roof. In a blink of an eye, Pu Yin had been captured by the two monks. They tied him up and took him to a lime pit to be burned.

The lime boiled, and the ropes snapped. Pu Yin, blind and with exposed bones, still managed to climb onto a short wall and stroke his ribs with his fleshless hand. A vegetable seller nearby saw this and was greatly alarmed, thinking it was a monster. He raised his hoe and struck him, instantly killing him and causing him to fall into the pool.

One of the two monks from Tianning Temple, named Gui Xiang, was skilled in the "remote striking" technique. He could carry two buckets of water on his shoulders and fly up to the nine-zhang-high (about 30 meters) roof of the main hall when it caught fire. I once strongly urged him to demonstrate his remote striking technique. He first closed the door, then extended his fist from more than twenty paces away. The door would immediately make a loud "砰" (pēng, bang) sound. He tried this three times, and it was always the same. I also wanted him to strike an ox and a dog, but the monk declined, clasping his hands in refusal. He said that he had once been a recorded admiral in the Qing army but had realized that life was just like this, so he had become a monk. Now, more than thirty years have passed. Gui Xiang has long since passed away, and his remote striking technique has no successor.

Against-the-Mouth Fungus 172

— Mai Lun

Our country's medical arts often involve extraordinary cures. Frequently, their efficacy defies rational explanation, approaching the miraculous. This is something Western medicine cannot comprehend. For example, the treatment of stubborn diseases using "Against-the-Mouth Fungus" is truly remarkable.

Tradition holds that Against-the-Mouth Fungus grows in desolate tombs between broken coffins. It is found as a fungal growth projecting from the underside of the coffin lid, positioned directly opposite the corpse's mouth. This substance is then acquired and said to cure all ailments, especially tuberculosis, with extraordinary results. I initially doubted this. I once asked a famous doctor about it. He said, "Although this medicine is not in the 'Compendium of Materia Medica,' I did see it once in the residence of a prominent official, Mr. Sheng. It has saved many lives. If we analyze it medically, it might be a crystallized product of Yin and Yang interacting." Later, I heard from a German doctor who said, "This is not impossible. The reason it can be obtained and used to treat stubborn diseases is probably accidental, like using talismans to cure illnesses. The illness might improve, but it's not actually due to the talisman." He then strongly criticized Chinese medicine for often misleading people with superstition, which seemed quite reasonable. So, the Against-the-Mouth Fungus is truly a miraculous substance that cannot be understood by ordinary reasoning.

Yesterday, I heard someone say that in the new fourteen-episode movie "Red Lotus Temple" by the Mingxing Film Company, an "Against-the-Mouth Fungus" serves as the main plot thread. It depicts two factions of swordsmen fighting over the fungus in a fierce and ever-changing battle, full of strange and varied occurrences. Initially, the Against-the-Mouth Fungus is obtained by an ape. From the ape, it becomes the object of a tortuous struggle. It presents a rather bizarre spectacle. Could this Against-the-Mouth Fungus truly be a miraculous object? This is truly incomprehensible.

I also remember hearing my grandmother say when I was young that my grandfather once suffered from tuberculosis. Later, a traveling doctor came and said he had an Against-the-Mouth Fungus and was willing to sell it for two hundred gold pieces. When asked where it came from, he said it was obtained from a desolate tomb outside Changsha. He then described the story of the Against-the-Mouth Fungus in vivid detail, just like the popular folk tales around Changsha and the strange stories written in irresponsible novels. Now, the film made by Mingxing is probably based on this story and embellished. With such varied and fantastical elements, it is bound to cause a sensation. There is nothing strange that doesn't exist in the world. The glittering silver screen should satisfy the curious.

The Anti-Communist Movement of Finnish Farmers (1) 173

— Liu Ceng, sent from Paris

(1) The Origin of the Lapua Movement

The recent anti-communist movement of Finnish farmers, known as the Lapua Movement (Lapua is the name of a small parish in Ostrobothnia, near Vaasa. The Finnish anti-communist movement first started there, hence the name), has attracted considerable attention in European public opinion. There are concerns that this movement could cause conflict between Finland and its eastern neighbor, Soviet Russia, thereby affecting European peace. Therefore, we cannot ignore it as a matter confined to a small Nordic country.

Before discussing the reasons for the emergence of this movement, it is necessary to examine the activities of the Communist Party in Finland. Finland's independence from Russia began in 1917. From this time onward, communist propaganda, directed and funded by the Moscow Third International, began its activities in Finland. While workers in major cities and industrial centers expressed deep sympathy, the intellectual class completely opposed it. The content of communist propaganda in Finland was the same as in other countries: opposition to the existing political, economic, religious, and military systems. On the platforms of parliament, in the deliberations of city councils, and in newspapers, communist members openly advocated for the overthrow of the current system by force. They also took advantage of Finland's system of freedom of publication and association to expand their propaganda.

However, the more intense the communist activities, the stricter the government's surveillance. Whenever necessary, strict measures were taken to suppress communist activity, attempting to fundamentally eliminate its propaganda. In 1923, all communist members of parliament were imprisoned. Other important communists were also severely punished. Moreover, the Communist Party was deemed an illegal party and prohibited from operating, setting a precedent.

Afterward, although most communist officials were imprisoned, new personnel, organized and trained in Russia, continuously infiltrated Finland to fill the vacancies. As a result, in the last parliamentary election, communist members, using the names of the Workers and Small Farmers Party (Parti des ouvriers et des paysans), obtained as many as 130,000 votes, occupying twenty-three seats in the two-hundred-seat parliament.

European Tour Correspondence (74) 174

— Liu Haisu

Pilgrimage to Italy Diary

(1) Introduction

In Europe, modern art is concentrated in Paris. People accustomed to seeing art in Paris are often dissatisfied when they see modern paintings, sculptures, or even architecture and crafts in any other country. However, the source of modern art is the Italian Renaissance. The art of the Renaissance, of course, follows the art of Greece and Rome. To study the Renaissance and earlier art, one must make a pilgrimage to Italy. I live in Paris, and I have more contact with modern art. Although I have seen Greek and Roman sculptures in the Louvre, and the works of Giotto, Botticelli, Fra Angelico, Giorgione, Masaccio, Filippo Lippi, Mantegna, Giovanni Bellini, Leonardo da Vinci, Raphael, Michelangelo, Titian, Tintoretto, and Veronese, I already had a slight understanding of the outline of Greek and Roman sculptures and Renaissance art. But I still felt it was not enough. I could not put it down. Recently, because I was determined to trace the source of modern art, I traced back in history, from modern art to the paintings of the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries in France, and then to the paintings of Spain and the Netherlands, all of which had direct or indirect relationships. To put it bluntly, all modern European art originates from the Renaissance. Because of this, my desire to visit Italy became even stronger. This kind of pilgrimage is more deeply ingrained in my mind than any other major event. This kind of feeling, not only is it in me, but all people who study art should at least think this way. If you like Delacroix, you should at least understand Rubens and Tintoretto. If you like E. Manet, you should at least understand Velazquez. If you want to understand Velazquez, you have to study Titian. If you like Cezanne, you should at least have seen Veronese and El Greco. Recently, from the works and books of various people, I have been pursuing the works of the glorious period of the Renaissance. Indeed, a pilgrimage to various parts of Italy is necessary to obtain a thorough understanding. If you want to see Tintoretto, Veronese, Titian, Tiepolo, then you should go to Venice. If you want to see the works of Michelangelo, Raphael, Botticelli, Angelico, Lippi, Andrea del Sarto, and da Vinci, you should go to Rome and Florence. Because their great works are abundantly contained in those small and bright gardens. Therefore, I departed from Paris on May 29th, 1919, to travel to various parts of Italy. But in this short period of one month, I went to four famous art cities: Rome, Florence, Venice, and Milan. I saw too many things. I wanted to pick up my pen to write many times, but I always felt like there was no way to start like a twenty-four history. Now I have to take my pilgrimage diary and publish it here first. In terms of art, what I feel is that I will write it out section by section after I have fully and seriously examined and checked it from all aspects. I am determined not to say a few abstract words in a general and superficial way to fill the role of an expert. In the end, after my pilgrimage to Italy, I have a beautiful and great faith in Italian art. This beautiful and great faith will not disappoint me for the rest of my life. This is what I can tell the readers first.

Silk and Tea: Wuxi Autumn Cocoons Still Have a Poor Harvest 191

This year's autumn silkworm rearing in the towns and villages of Wuxi has approximately doubled compared to last year. Unfortunately, due to adverse weather conditions, coupled with uneven breeding, the harvest is still poor. Statistics on the cocoon production in the four villages show that although there are five to six-tenths of a yield, the cocoon quality is poor, and only about 30% is suitable for the sales channels of silk factories. Cocoons have been successively weighed in each road cocoon bank, but the amount received by each bank is limited. Now all the fresh cocoons received are dried and hired to be transported to Shanghai.

New York, however, due to the stock market crash, silk sales in various silk weaving factories were stagnant. Silk telegrams yesterday did not change, and the market atmosphere was sluggish. The silk market was completely stalled.

Tea Market: A Complete Collapse 193

Yesterday's tea market transactions suddenly became quiet. Zhenmei green tea from the coming road village, except for the core-extracted goods which sold slightly, the rest was sluggish. The general market also stopped again. There were no major transactions of Zhenmei, Xiumei and other goods. The market was quite a picture of total failure. However, since the Association's market yesterday, preparations have been made for action on the black teas of Lianghu Qining. Public apprehension has been slightly lessened.

A Large Batch of Grey Shirting and Fine Cloth is Offered 194

The cotton cloth market in this factory was slightly weak yesterday, especially the fine cloth, which was the softest. The reason for this was the sluggish actual sales, and the factory offered a large batch of it, Blue Chicken offered 1,500 pieces, priced at 6 taels and 5 qian and a half, and the forward months of January, February, March and April, Caiqiu Yanghe Blue Double Fish etc. were all priced at around 6 taels and 8 qian, amounting to 4,000 to 5,000 pieces, with the same forward dates, so public apprehension suddenly increased. Spot goods fell across the board yesterday, by 5 cents, Blue Flying Fish was at 7 taels 1 qian and 2.5 fen, Caiqiu at 6 taels and 8 qian and a half, and Yanghe at 6 taels 8 qian and 2.5 fen. Among the coarse cloth, Sanlu and SanTu continued to rise, yesterday costing 4 taels and 9 qian, but Ren Zhong was still at 4 taels and 7 qian and a half, and fine twill has risen all the more, Yanghe has reached 7 taels 3 qian and 2.5 fen, and Blue Double Fish 6 taels 9 qian and 7.5 fen.

The East-West Pingtou Market was still firm yesterday, but East goods had risen too quickly for several days, and actual sales were slightly sluggish. Qingdao and Tianjin gangs had somewhat come to an end. Yesterday, only flower straight tribute woolen cloth and floral patterns had some transactions. The trend of Sichuan Gang's big flower Yuehua velvet turned brisk, with telegrams adding more than 100 pieces in demand, so it continued to rise by 2.5 cents. Yesterday, Da Ji Long and Tianshang Qi Ba were sold for 2 qian and 7 li and a half, and White Peony sold out at 2 qian and 5 li, Huimei Pique also rose yesterday, Huxinting Da Huiwen already requires 2 qian and 5 fen and 2.5 li, Boat Beauty 2 qian and 5 fen, and Lieyan Xiao Jiawen sold out at 2 qian and 7 fen. There was not much change in fine Pique and Straight Tribute woolen cloth, and West goods such as bleached cloth etc. were quite deserted in sales due to the unsuitable season. Taixi satin, Yuanchou and Chouben Street had transactions yesterday.

Hardware: East White Iron Suddenly Rises 195

The East white iron market suddenly rose by two to three cents yesterday. It is estimated that a 3'7" sheet is worth 1 tael and 1 qian and 4 fen, and a 3'6" sheet 9 qian and 1 fen. It is said that this price increase is actually because the East exchange rate is fixed and unchanged, and that arrivals are few and prices are high, and there is also some impact from this. However, upon hearing this news, the Ke gangs scrambled to buy spot goods, in order to prevent prices from rising again. It is said that 6,000 to 7,000 sheets have already been offered for sale yesterday, and those buying were the gangs in the Yangtze River inland and Fujian, and in addition the Nanjing Hangjiahu gangs also bought a sprinkling.
